  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9bec6461-3b68-437a-807d-5fe726135ca6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText836431748324620641" style="display:none"><b>BEWARE! THE PLANET IS WOUNDED... THE GEMINI ARE RISING AND OUR TIME ON EARTH IS LIMITED</b><br /><br />Angry at the human race and its methodical destruction of her resources, Mother Earth recruits souls who have just left their bodies to serve Her, and turns them against humanity. Gemini, a clan of paranormal beings, picked from these possessed humans, emerges. A powerful, rising force proceeds to carry out Mother Nature’s plan to systematically destroy towns, cities, states… and eventually, the world. Amidst the chaos, a forbidden relationship between a human girl, Violette, and Onyx, a lead Gemini, begins. They will both find themselves in the middle of a revolutionary war that will either save, or destroy our world.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591558605?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica O&#39;Gorek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica O&#39;Gorek" href="/user/show/14991002-jessica-o-gorek">Jessica O&#39;Gorek</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_624683663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624683663" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7569687-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563752671p2/7569687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624683663?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/7569687-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624683663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9853309973301018463">(This review can be found on my blog <a href='' rel='nofollow noopener'>The (Mis)Adventures of a Twenty-Something Year Old Girl</a>).<br/><br/><br/>I thought the blurb to this book sounded super interesting and different. I was hoping this book would be interested, and luckily, it was.<br/><br/>When a human who polluted the Earth dies, they become a Gemini and belong to mother Earth. Onyx is a Gemini. His mission is to help destroy the human race. Everything is going smoothly until he comes across Violette, a 16 year old human girl. Geminis aren't really sup</span>
  <span id="freeText9853309973301018463" style="display:none">(This review can be found on my blog <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener">The (Mis)Adventures of a Twenty-Something Year Old Girl</a>).<br /><br /><br />I thought the blurb to this book sounded super interesting and different. I was hoping this book would be interested, and luckily, it was.<br /><br />When a human who polluted the Earth dies, they become a Gemini and belong to mother Earth. Onyx is a Gemini. His mission is to help destroy the human race. Everything is going smoothly until he comes across Violette, a 16 year old human girl. Geminis aren't really supposed to feel anything, yet Onyx feels drawn to Violette. He possess the body of an acolyte to befriend her. What follows will make Onyx question everything he's ever known.<br /><br />I didn't know what to expect with this title. I figured it had something to do with Ethereals, but that was all I got from the title. After reading the book, the title matches what the book's about.<br /><br />I'm not really a fan of the cover. To me, the cover makes it seem like the book wouldn't be good which isn't the case at all. I just think that the cover could've been made to entice readers to pick it up.<br /><br />The world building is good, but there are a few things that left me confused such as how the book says that Geminis don't have feelings. However, a few of the Geminis had feelings such as worry and anger. Onyx seemed to have more feelings than all the Geminis. Hopefully, why Onyx is the way he is will be explained in the next book. Another thing that made me confused was the fact that Geminis are ethereal beings. However, they were able to move things, pick things up, etc in their natural form. Perhaps I just missed something along the way. Oh, and one more thing. I was confused whether these things were demons or something else. I get that they're Geminis, yet it mentions in the book about how exorcisms seem to work on the Geminis. I also don't really get why the Geminis wanted to start with churches first. I get that they wanted to start small, but why pick churches? Other than those things, I enjoyed the world building.<br /><br />The pacing started off a little bit slow but quickly picked up. Before I knew it, I was quickly sucked into the world of Geminis versus humans. Every chapter ending left me wanting to know more, so I'd quickly start the next chapter. Even the ending of this book left me wanting more.<br /><br />When it comes to humans versus something that wants to wipe them from the face of the Earth, it's been done before. However, Miss O'Gorek brings a refreshing twist on the common theme. I loved how it was beings who were angry at the humans for not taking care of the Earth that wanted them gone. It may sound like a hippie story line, and I thought it was going to be just that at first, but it quickly turns into a sound plot line.<br /><br />The characters were written fabulously! I loved Violette. I loved her vulnerability and her child like innocence. She is a very naive girl, but this is only because she's been stuck inside an orphanage for mostly her whole life. The only problem I had with her is how she couldn't tell that something was up with Slate especially after what had happened to her. I enjoyed the character of Onyx. It was interesting to see how he wrestled with what he wanted and what he was supposed to do. I hated the bishop...not because he was poorly written but because he was just so mean! The author did a fantastic job of making us hate the bishop.<br /><br />The dialogue was really interesting, and I enjoyed reading about all the characters. I especially enjoyed Onyx's point of view and dialogue the most. There are some sexual references though, so if that's not really your cup of tea, just be warned. However, the sexual references are mild.<br /><br />Overall, Ethereal Fury (Gemini Rising #1) is an interesting read that will leave readers wanting more (in a good way). It certainly left me wanting more. I will definitely be reading the next book in the series.<br /><br />I'd recommend this book to everyone aged 16+ who want to get sucked in to a great read.<br /><br />(I was given a paperback copy of this title for free from the author in exchange for a fair and honest review).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9853309973301018463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_720127586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720127586" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5408262-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304972469p2/5408262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720127586?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/5408262-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5408262-barbara?shelf=books-with-beautiful-covers">books-with-beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5408262-barbara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5408262-barbara?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5408262-barbara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720127586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10387482787099923190"><i>**A free copy of this book was provided by author in exchange for an honest review**</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380292674ra/682220.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have mixed feelings about this book. I did like it, but not the whole book. For me, it was really hard getting into the story at the beginning. I was confused and sometimes even bored and almost gave up on it a couple of times, but what made me keep going was the writing. The other half of the book was really captivating and I have read it in one breath. At the end, I was positively surprised. I had a hard time</span>
  <span id="freeText10387482787099923190" style="display:none"><i>**A free copy of this book was provided by author in exchange for an honest review**</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380292674ra/682220.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have mixed feelings about this book. I did like it, but not the whole book. For me, it was really hard getting into the story at the beginning. I was confused and sometimes even bored and almost gave up on it a couple of times, but what made me keep going was the writing. The other half of the book was really captivating and I have read it in one breath. At the end, I was positively surprised. I had a hard time deciding how to rate this book. I have decided to give it three stars because it was good and I saw a lot of potential there. I really hope that the sequel will be better, because, honestly, I do love giving five stars to books, I hate writing shitty reviews and I usually don't even rate them. But some things just didn't work out for me. It could have been better. Maybe I just had unrealistic expectations because of all those five stars reviews. <br> <br>First, I have to admit that gorgeous cover is what attracted me to this book in the first place. I loved the concept of revenge of Mother Earth and creating an army of Gemini to eliminate all human race. It was something new and really refreshing. At the same time, I felt little disappointed because Gemini were possessing humans and the Church considered them demons and I must say that is an old thing! I didn't like that they were turned into demons. I don't know, in my mind, Mother Earth is a powerful being who is perfectly capable of destroying human kind by simply causing a natural disasters and voila the bad guys are gone. But we all need a little drama in our life and what' s better than killing your abusers little by little like they have done to you. Maybe Mother wanted to savor a victory slowly so she could enjoy it much more. I prefer to think that way. I got over all that demon thing later. I got used to it, and it doesn't bother as much as before. <br> <br><u>Characters</u><br> <br><b>Slate</b> <br><br><i>"What an odd thing for her to say. She was a sixteen-year-old girl in a Catholic orphanage. Surviving in a place like this should be as easy as breathing."</i><br> <br>Obviously, he said that. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390080330ra/8140293.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Violette is just too smart for him. I still don't get why she fell in love with him. Well, it's not like she had too much of a choice, to be honest. He was controlled and sheltered from the outside world by Father Darius and although I liked him a lot because he was so nice person and besides how could you not like a loyal, caring, innocent and loving man like him. I hated Oliver/Onyx at the beginning so I was team Slate first. I was, because I'm not anymore. I got bored of him. Yes, I fell for the bad guy I'm humbly admitting. But in Slate's defense I have to say that guy never left the church so it's no wonder he is the way he is. <br> <br><i>"I’m busy studying and learning verses. I don’t have time to be mean, or be a criminal.”</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390259572ra/8178337.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Oliver/Onyx</b> <br><br>He was so despicable, such a greedy man, I was happy when he died. Then he was turned into Gemini with a mission to save the world from the people like he used to be. That confused the hell of me. Why were they after churches and not after humans that had contributed to the pollution the most. Maybe I just missed something? He fell so hard for Violette for no obvious reason. He was drawn to her and even spared her life and broke the rules. Forbidden love? Yes, I like that a lot and I kind of grow attached to him. I knew he was an asshole, but gave him the second chance because he was very good to my dear Violette. Although one time he wasn't good to her and I know that I was supposed to hate him for that but I loved him instead. Ha, like I have said already, I love little drama. <br> <br><i>"Sweet, innocent, untouched, yet here she was, a deliberately seductive display of what should have been absolutely private. That she would risk her safety like this made him crazy, but he simply could not take his eyes off of her yet."</i> <br> <br>Yes, she will be the death to you :)<br> <br> <br><b>Violette</b> <br> <br>Poor girl, doesn't wanna be a nun and had to lead a life of misery. For Violette the orphanage was like a prison. That safe life was not for her, too safety also meant too boredom. Violette was really mature for her age and she perceived the things around her very well. She was the only character I liked from the beginning till the end. She was innocent and naive, but it didn't bother me as much as usually for a reason I cannot find. Maybe I was just in a mood for a character likes her. I liked her innocence, but I saw a lot of inner strength in her and that made me love her even more. <br> <br><i>"What person in her right mind would want to cuddle with an unearthly since could not be defined? Me, that’s who. Okay, so she was crazy, now what? She could just enjoy the lunacy instead of having these question-and-answer periods."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390259572ra/8178338.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>She was a reckless a lot, but I'm glad she was, because I enjoyed her scenes with Onyx a lot and I'm looking forward to see how their relationship will develops further. <br> <br><b>Plot</b> <br>Ha, you wish! I'm not going to say a word about that, I don't wanna spoil it for the future readers. <br> <br>To end, I liked it, not as much as I thought I would, but still it was an enjoyable read. I would recommend it to fans of paranormal romance, because this is really something different. Getting into the book was hard for me, but I can promise that it gets better. And to warn you all, there is a cliffhanger at the end. I have a love-hate relationship with them. I had a sneak peek into the first chapter of the sequel. it ended with cliffhanger too. I mean, really? That was so mean. Dear Jessica, please write faster, because I'm dying to see what will happen next. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380743475ra/3118206.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10387482787099923190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_606573336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606573336" />
    <a title="Emily Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13045626-emily-anne"><img alt="Emily Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533593667p2/13045626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606573336?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Anne" href="/user/show/13045626-emily-anne">Emily Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606573336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2322050921392641219">Ethereal Fury (which I still just call Gemini Rising most of the time) was a wonderful read that had me speeding along the pages in a very different adventure from most YA novels. Gemini was such a good idea and I am anxious to learn more about them in the sequel, Gemini in Retrograde.<br/><br/>The characters that went along with the wonderful ideas were also nothing short of spectacular. Gemini such as Onyx and his sister Lilly, were created in just the right way. They were cold but it seemed like they c</span>
  <span id="freeText2322050921392641219" style="display:none">Ethereal Fury (which I still just call Gemini Rising most of the time) was a wonderful read that had me speeding along the pages in a very different adventure from most YA novels. Gemini was such a good idea and I am anxious to learn more about them in the sequel, Gemini in Retrograde.<br /><br />The characters that went along with the wonderful ideas were also nothing short of spectacular. Gemini such as Onyx and his sister Lilly, were created in just the right way. They were cold but it seemed like they could show affection and maybe even feel guilt.<br /><br />For a more detailed explanation of Gemini, I should say that they are paranormal beings under the wing of Mother Earth, who is, as stated in the synopsis, angry at our people for polluting and causing the slow destruction of her natural resources. Gemini are meant to destroy the human race, although the twist is that the Gemini were humans first.<br /><br />Most of Gemini Rising (Ethereal Fury) was spent in the midst of a church. This church has knowledge of the Gemini, although it was very limited. Onyx, a Gemini, decides to try to figure out exactly what and how much the church knows. The church setting is something I found surprisingly intriguing. The ideas of priests, nuns, orphans, confessions, and other churchly things among the gemini spread a layer of suspense and a dreary, nearly desperate background to the story as the church tries to ward of the "demons". At this point may I point out that in the book I was appalled by human actions as well as gemini?<br /><br />Other important characters in the church include Slate, Violette, Father Darius, and Bishop Phillips. Violette was sweet and had character growth, as did somewhat cautois Slate, although he has a lot to learn. I am not sure what to think of Father Darius but I will say right now I am not a fan of Phillips. And, of course, the romance. I thought the chemistry between Onyx and Violette was quite good. I do hope in the next book we get to hear more real conversations between them. I am not sure what to think of Onyx, as he has done some evil things . (I mean, he is a Gemini. But does that excuse him from everything he has done. Uh-uh, Not even close. If he is to even think of redeeming himself he will have to work mighty hard to please me.) I did like how real and vivid his character seemed though. I really enjoyed the chapters from his view point.<br /><br />This book is truly unique and the ideas presented were fresh and different. Jessica O'Gorek not only didn't miss the mark, she arrowed her story straight into the center. I would not hesitate to recommend this book to anybody, teen or older, looking for a different, beautiful book in the paranormal/supernatural genre. <br /><br />Overall this book earned 4 stars. I really, really enjoyed Etereal Fury, also known as Gemini Rising. The sequel cannot be released fast enough!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2322050921392641219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_645736471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645736471" />
    <a title="Daniela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5532374-daniela"><img alt="Daniela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375821577p2/5532374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645736471?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniela" href="/user/show/5532374-daniela">Daniela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645736471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16081417545245643895">Ethereal Fury (Gemini Rising) is a unique masterpiece I was not expecting. The first couple of pages didn't exactly draw me in, though. While the concept was definitely interesting, it was a little bizarre for my taste and it took me a while to adapt to that change, but that's just about the only setback in this book.<br/>I was not so used to seeing Mother Earth personified in such a pissed off manner, but it was pretty cool. And when the churches and the Catholic orphanages came in, I started to wor</span>
  <span id="freeText16081417545245643895" style="display:none">Ethereal Fury (Gemini Rising) is a unique masterpiece I was not expecting. The first couple of pages didn't exactly draw me in, though. While the concept was definitely interesting, it was a little bizarre for my taste and it took me a while to adapt to that change, but that's just about the only setback in this book.<br />I was not so used to seeing Mother Earth personified in such a pissed off manner, but it was pretty cool. And when the churches and the Catholic orphanages came in, I started to worry that this would take a religious turn-about. I'm not so comfortable with those. Thankfully, the story stayed within its line of sci-fi (added with a romantic twist, of course). My doubts on this book instantly vanished, I was hooked before I even reached the half-way mark. The characters were written beautifully, the plot had some very unexpected twists, and the level of refreshment this book provided was like a spa getaway. It had it's cliche moments, don't get me wrong, but they seemed vague most of the time.<br /><br />Character-wise, Onyx was... different. For starters, he's not human, he's a Gemini. And Geminis are like thin wisps of smoke. They can posses human bodies, but without a body, they aren't much. Onyx himself starts out as an unfeeling jerk and stays like that for a while, but there's this sweet side to him that bubbled to the surface (especially when Violette was around). Seeing things mostly through his point of view was exciting. I liked the way his struggle towards humanity were executed. And his jealousy. ;)<br />Although, the character that surprised me the most was Violette.<br />See, Violette isn't the sort of female character that I usually root for. She was uncommonly naive for a 16 year old (but she spent most of her life in an orphanage so that was understandable) and incredibly vulnerable. I just don't have patience for these sorts of characters no matter how reasonable their excuse is. I get annoyed with them easily and it doesn't take much to make me hate them. So one of the main reasons why I love this book is the way Violette's character was written. I wanted to hate her, really I did. She was the sort of girl who was abnormally beautiful and didn't even know it, that's the biggest cliche ever! But seeing things mostly through Onyx's perspective was the smartest way to deflect my hatred. <br />The romance between them was slow and mainly driven by lust. It was a little discomforting that Onyx was a middle-aged man when he died and he was crushing on a teenager, but I got over that. He wasn't human anymore, he could only posses human bodies. <br /><br />Overall, I wasn't expecting to like Ethereal Fury as much as I did. Besides, the fact that Violette's character caught me off guard, the entire story was deliciously unique. Delicious because I was hungry for something new, and now that I got it, I'm starving to have the rest. <br />But be warned, the ending is one of THOSE. It's not exactly a cliffhanger, but one book won't do. Uh-uh, I need the rest and I need it now (spoiled much, I know).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16081417545245643895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_710818944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/710818944" />
    <a title="coconutsnbutts (♫ נєѕѕι¢α  ♪)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19520582-coconutsnbutts"><img alt="coconutsnbutts (♫ נєѕѕι¢α  ♪)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547963390p2/19520582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/710818944?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="coconutsnbutts (♫ נєѕѕι¢α  ♪)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="coconutsnbutts (♫ נєѕѕι¢α  ♪)" href="/user/show/19520582-coconutsnbutts">coconutsnbutts (♫ נєѕѕι¢α  ♪)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19520582-coconutsnbutts?shelf=can-she-be-any-whinier">can-she-be-any-whinier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19520582-coconutsnbutts?shelf=are-you-serious-right-now">are-you-serious-right-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19520582-coconutsnbutts?shelf=books-ive-reviewed">books-ive-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19520582-coconutsnbutts?shelf=expected-it-to-be-better">expected-it-to-be-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19520582-coconutsnbutts?shelf=meh">meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer710818944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11357047915013970427"><b>
  <i>"The Mother is our ruler. She is all powerful and merciless, as merciless as the humans have been to her. We have been given a chance to repent. Our human sins will be wiped clean, we will be forgiven, but first, we must complete our mission."</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>3 stars.</i><br/><br/>*I received this book free in exchange for an honest review*<br/><br/>I was so hyped to read this book. I remember hearing about it, then finding the R2R thread a month late but still requesting a copy, and then being SO happy when Ms. O'Gorek generously </span>
  <span id="freeText11357047915013970427" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"The Mother is our ruler. She is all powerful and merciless, as merciless as the humans have been to her. We have been given a chance to repent. Our human sins will be wiped clean, we will be forgiven, but first, we must complete our mission."</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>3 stars.</i><br /><br />*I received this book free in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br />I was so hyped to read this book. I remember hearing about it, then finding the R2R thread a month late but still requesting a copy, and then being SO happy when Ms. O'Gorek generously gave me one. I expected big things; I mean, this was something different for once. We're all sick of the cliche vampires and werewolves, right? <br /><br />Unfortunately, this book failed to meet my expectations. But I'll start this review off on a positive note...<br /><br /><br /><i>THE GOOD:</i><br /><br /><b>The concept.</b> I reeeaaally enjoyed the concept of the book. Little god-like creatures, sent by Mother Earth, to finally come and kill off our godforsaken, worthless, trouble making, human selves (that's how we're portrayed, anyways). Whats better than that? <br /><br /><b>How Mother Earth was portrayed.</b> Can you say Bitch, with a capital B? Yeah, that's Mother Earth. She was mean (for completely understandable reasons) and she got shit done. I loved that. <br /><br />Aaaaaaannnnddddd moving on.<br /><br /><br /><i>THE BAD:</i><br /><br /><b>The writing.</b> It didn't flow well and there were numerous grammatical errors. I came across multiple misspellings, run on sentences, and improper usage of commas. But that's nothing that can't be fixed with a bit of editing, However, the book lacked much needed details and descriptions of the settings, surroundings, and minor characters. I grew tired of hearing descriptions of the 3 main characters; I just want to know what the building looked like, what the surrounding area looked like, and most importantly what the supporting characters looked like. But no, all I got was what Onyx, Slate, and Ms. So Fucking Perfect (aka Violet) looked like. Which brings on my next issue...<br /><br /><b>Violet.</b> Violet. Oh, darling, sweet, innocent, perfect Violet. I was so SICK of reading about how Violet's eye were purple, and how her hair was lusciously dark and long and beautiful, and how apparently her shit doesn't stink. Oh god by the middle of the book I was so tired of Violet this and Violet that that I was tempted to just give up. She was portrayed to be so innocent and young, but she was trying to get in Slate's/Onyx's pants just as much as he wanted to get in her's. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She goes skinny dipping in a pond, and when Onyx/Slate find her she wants to be like "how did you find me?! turn around while I get dressed I'm suddenly so modest!!" but not even 5 pages later when Onyx/Slate asks her why she went out when he told her not to (or something, I forgot exactly what he said) she simply replies "I knew you'd come." darling innocent perfect little frail Violet, did you go out skinny dipping because you "knew he'd come"? That's how it seems to me! you diiirrrrtttyyy girl. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Oh, and don't even get me started on the sexual tension in this book. Either Violet was constantly thinking about banging Slate/Onyx or vice versa. And then they would finally get together, and be ready to do it, and Slate/Onyx would back off. This happened like 3 times. Look its realy not that hard, you either do the dirty or you don't, but constantly being on the whim about it was ANNOYING.<br /><br /><b>Misleading synopsis.</b> I was told this book had <i>"a revolutionary war that will either save, or destroy our world."</i> I didn't get this. :( All I got was a dramatic romance between a Gemini and a human. No action, nothing. /sadface.<br /><br />Oh and also, I couldn't decide whether I liked Onyx or not. He was a strong, independent character, but I feel like his love for Violet was more of a sick obsession. He had stalker-like habits that I found to be unnerving. <br /><br />Well that's really all I have to say. Solid 3 stars. In conclusion, the majority of the problems in this book aren't terrible, and they can be fixed with a strong sequel that contains character evolution, better writing, and a more defined plot. I plan on reading the sequel when it comes out, because the sample chapter I read had me hooked. <br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>THAT IS ALL.</b>
</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11357047915013970427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_652845760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9347943-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439488438p2/9347943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/652845760?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/9347943-brittany">Brittany</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17738490-ethereal-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652845760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14585360437891521435"><i> Review also appears on my blog <a href='http://www.misadventureswonderland.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'> Misadventures in Wonderland</a> </i><br/><br/>Well, I have been procrastinating big time on finishing this review. I enjoyed the book, shockingly more than I anticipated. The main issue is I have not exactly been sure what to say. My initial reaction to the book was just...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380379700ra/735973.gif' width='250' height='143' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853669.gif' width='400' height='258' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396207ra/763510.gif' width='400' height='234' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Pretty much the entire premise of the novel is Mother Nature is ticked we are destroying the world, so she is fighting back. The Christian church is on the front lines of the attack. So its almost like a basic g</span>
  <span id="freeText14585360437891521435" style="display:none"><i> Review also appears on my blog <a href="http://www.misadventureswonderland.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener"> Misadventures in Wonderland</a> </i><br><br>Well, I have been procrastinating big time on finishing this review. I enjoyed the book, shockingly more than I anticipated. The main issue is I have not exactly been sure what to say. My initial reaction to the book was just...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380379700ra/735973.gif" width="250" height="143" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853669.gif" width="400" height="258" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396207ra/763510.gif" width="400" height="234" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pretty much the entire premise of the novel is Mother Nature is ticked we are destroying the world, so she is fighting back. The Christian church is on the front lines of the attack. So its almost like a basic good vs evil, except in this instance is the evil truly evil or is it correcting acts of evil?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853670.gif" width="400" height="429" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Basically, the story begins with an oil tycoon and all of the wrong he does. Then he dies and comes back as a Gemini, which is an ethereal being made of a wispy, smoke like material. They also want to destroy humans. The Church refers to them as demons and exorcisms work on them, but I'm not positive if that is what they are technically. Honestly, it is not a far stretch from a man that was bad in life to become an evil creature after death. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853671.gif" width="400" height="429" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then the story flips to the protagonist, Violette. She is an extremely naive girl of 16 who is being raised in a Catholic orphanage after a fire claimed her parent's lives. The nuns take care of the orphans (who are all females apparently) while the priests go about their daily lives. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853672.gif" width="400" height="362" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, the daily lives of priests is demon hunting. Enter Slate, a young man who is a priest in training (or just the protege of a priest) who gets sucked into this whole Supernatural-esque down with the demons thing. Which is pretty bad ass if I must say so myself. The story then flips back to Onyx the Gemini and his whole must destroy the humans evilness. That is, until he see Violette and starts creeping on her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853673.gif" width="166" height="166" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To avoid spoilers, let's just say a lot of chaos ensues including a love triangle between Slate/Onyx/Violette. There is also a douche bag of a bishop. Seriously, I hate him more than the Gemini who are created to be the evil ones of the story. Bishop does something to Violette but Slate puts an end to it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853674.gif" width="400" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The entire story concludes with the mother of all cliff hangers. Lucky for me, my copy had an excerpt of the beginning of the next novel so that helped make it not as rough for me. Over-all it was an entertaining novel that I am eagerly awaiting the sequel to.<br><br>This next area is spoiler filled, be warned.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ok, I feel very conflicted with the whole Slate/Onyx and Violette thing. Slate never seemed to have an interest in Violette before Onyx started possessing him. As for Onyx, is he not still a middle aged person in spirit form or did dying erase all of that and make him younger? It seems like with the disappearance of his memories also made his age regress but I am not positive. It just bothered me most of the time. As for everyone being team Slate or team Onyx, I'm pretty much team Violette. I want her to mature and age as a character before even beginning to think of either of them romantically. I feel as if her character can become lost easily within either of the guys. Oh, everyone also exhibited major stalker vibes during the novel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427044ra/853675.gif" width="400" height="282" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I really hope the love triangle does not end up with a ton of angst and characters pining after one another. Otherwise, I am very hopeful for this series  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_745563729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/745563729" />
    <a title="Kimber Wheaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16667146-kimber-wheaton"><img alt="Kimber Wheaton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383774408p2/16667146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/745563729?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimber Wheaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimber Wheaton" href="/user/show/16667146-kimber-wheaton">Kimber Wheaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16667146-kimber-wheaton?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745563729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer259045688574084895">*I received this book from the author in exchange for an honest review*<br/><br/>I was immediately drawn to the blurb for <i>Gemini Rising</i>. The concept is so intriguing and not something I've run into before. This is the first book of a series, and features an abrupt ending. I'm not exaggerating. It ends in the middle of a scene, in the middle of a conversation, and just as it was starting to get really interesting. I hate being left dangling, like the computer died and rather than finish the novel, it was p</span>
  <span id="freeText259045688574084895" style="display:none">*I received this book from the author in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br />I was immediately drawn to the blurb for <i>Gemini Rising</i>. The concept is so intriguing and not something I've run into before. This is the first book of a series, and features an abrupt ending. I'm not exaggerating. It ends in the middle of a scene, in the middle of a conversation, and just as it was starting to get really interesting. I hate being left dangling, like the computer died and rather than finish the novel, it was published as is. There's a preview for the next book in the series, and it does pick up in the exact spot this one ended.<br /><br />The prologue is strange. Oliver designs oil production equipment that is destroying the environment. When he dies, he is taken to Mother Earth to perform penance for his sins against Her. So we've got this old man that's turned into one of the Gemini, Mother Earth's warriors against humanity. His new name is Onyx and he becomes taken with teenage orphan Violette when he seeks to infiltrate the church where she resides. I couldn't stop thinking of him as this crotchety old man, though he has no memoires of his past and is no longer human. Strange indeed.<br /><br />The entire story concept is interesting, but I was left with so much confusion and lots of unanswered questions. The romance between Onyx and Violette is just plain creepy, considering he's possessing a human being to be near her. His obsession is not normal for a Gemini, the fact of which he is well aware. I find it ironic that Oliver. the human, held nothing but disdain for humanity and the environment, yet when he is reborn he develops an unnatural obsession with one.<br /><br /><i>Gemini Rising</i> is suitable for everyone high school and up. If you are looking for a unique concept consider adding it to your to-read list.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="259045688574084895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2373465741154835145" style="display:none">Given the story and what it withholds, the book held me captive with wanting to know what was to come. There are some areas where the story has a science fiction feel to it and at first I was not willing to turn another page. There were a few scenes with the Gemini that were a bit gruesome even for my imagination. The cover itself doesn't give away the story but does represent it quite well. There is so much compacted into this book that you never know what will come next or where the author will take you with each turn of the page. <br /> <br />The characters have a battle to fight, not only with others but within themselves. They are well developed and likeable. The romance that comes into play was a refresher but found in the midst of battle and war makes it hard. Onyx and Violette come together in the most unimaginable place and time.<br /> <br />Our precious Earth is being destroyed, used up and damaged.... But ever wonder how Earth would feel being neglected? Wanting back what has been taken - Earth fires back and sets out to destroy the very beings that have taken advantage of her.</span>

I fell in love with Onyx who is this brutishly beautiful character who does have a heart but it takes a lot to get into his hard shell. This story has serious undertones that make you think and touched my heart in ways I didn't think a book could. This is a 10 star book on my list and I know I will be assigning it to my daughter and sons to read, Jessica is such a talented wordstress and she knows how to tell a story for sure! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_697645638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/697645638" />
    <a title="J.Aleksandr Wootton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1027995-j-aleksandr-wootton"><img alt="J.Aleksandr Wootton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444685096p2/1027995.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697645638?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.Aleksandr Wootton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.Aleksandr Wootton" href="/user/show/1027995-j-aleksandr-wootton">J.Aleksandr Wootton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">readers of YA paranormal romance</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to J.Aleksandr by: </span>
      Jessica O'Gorek
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1027995-j-aleksandr-wootton?shelf=caveat-lector">caveat-lector</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697645638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2924921357093823478">**Disclaimer: the author provided me with a free copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br/><br/>Had I realized this was a romance novel, I would not have agreed to review it. I've read just enough romance novels to know I don't like the genre - at all. So keep that in mind!<br/><br/>While the novel's description does mention romance, it places a much more interesting sci-fi concept front-and-center. It's an exciting description and I was quite intrigued by it. Unfortunately, <i>Ethereal Fury</i> spends almos</span>
  <span id="freeText2924921357093823478" style="display:none">**Disclaimer: the author provided me with a free copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />Had I realized this was a romance novel, I would not have agreed to review it. I've read just enough romance novels to know I don't like the genre - at all. So keep that in mind!<br /><br />While the novel's description does mention romance, it places a much more interesting sci-fi concept front-and-center. It's an exciting description and I was quite intrigued by it. Unfortunately, <i>Ethereal Fury</i> spends almost no time exploring its sci-fi ideas. Instead (as is typical of romance novels), the book fleshes out its setting as thinly as it possibly can in order to move on to the, well, actual flesh.<br /><br />So I felt a little bait-and-switched. If you happen to be a reader who likes both the bait and the switch, that won't be a problem for you; but for someone who cares more about exploring a new world/concept then reading about yet another teen romance, this was a little annoying. <br /><br />But to be fair, there was only one real gap in the exposition: for some reason the Gemini, who are otherwise practically all-powerful in their ethereal form, cannot enter buildings owned by the Catholic Church without possessing a living person. This is never explained. Is God real in this setting? Does this fictional Catholic Church have some other source of supernatural power? We're never told.<br /><br />Unfortunately this is a big gap, since the premise of the whole story hinges on this fact.<br /><br />I have one other objection, this time on the romance end. There's a sexual assault scene by our male protagonist, Slate, against the female protagonist, Violette. <br /><br />(Slate is possessed by the <i>other</i> male protagonist, Onyx, at the time. Yeah, there's an awkward supernatural love triangle thing going on.)<br /><br />Although the scene itself is relatively tame, and the romance throughout the book is generally kept to the "sweet-and-sensual" realm, there's a broader cultural issue here. <br /><br />These kinds of scenes resonate with readers because the supernatural possession (the "excuse") acts as a metaphor for sexual assault by male teens who are (or at least feel) possessed by their hormones. Anyone who has had such an experience, male or female, enjoys reading a story where a similar experience is redeemed.<br /><br />But in the United States, one in four college-age women has been sexually assaulted at least once since she turned 14. On average, a woman is raped every 2 minutes, and most of the time the rapist is someone she knows. (Read <a href="http://www.oneinfourusa.org/statistics.php" rel="nofollow noopener">statistics</a>.)<br /><br />My problem with this scene, and with most romance novels that include similar scenes, is Violette's/the female lead's response. In the stories our female protagonist forgives, and resumes her romantic relationship with, her attacker - and things work out. It might make for titillating reading, but it's the exact opposite of good advice for survivors and at-risk readers. <br /><br />It's not that happily-ever-afters aren't possible. It's that happily-ever-after <i>with that person</i> isn't.<br /><br />In reality, we should practice a one-strike-and-you're-out policy. Nobody should ever return to a partner (or potential partner) who has been abusive, even once, ever, for any reason. Yet people do, all the time. It's happening somewhere right now, as I write this, and somewhere else again, as you're reading it.<br /><br />I'm not saying romance novels are to blame - that's not it at all. And I really am sorry to soapbox <i>Gemini Rising</i> like this, because it's a fine story that has clearly been enjoyed by many people. But we do have a serious problem with sexual assault in this and probably every country, and it's difficult not to conclude that the romance genre, in general, mishandles the topic and treats it far too lightly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2924921357093823478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_654467487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654467487" />
    <a title="Michelle Willms" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18489454-michelle-willms"><img alt="Michelle Willms" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408373021p2/18489454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/654467487?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Willms" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Willms" href="/user/show/18489454-michelle-willms">Michelle Willms</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18489454-michelle-willms?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18489454-michelle-willms?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18489454-michelle-willms?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18489454-michelle-willms?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer654467487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4899676848595926190">Gemini Rising by Jessica O’Gorek<br/>Gemini Rising: Ethereal Fury by Jessica O’Gorek<br/>MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS <br/>The main premise in this book is that Mother Earth is furious at humanity’s blatant disregard for the health of the planet and has decided to wipe out mankind. She recruits newly departed souls, generally those who were evil during their lives, and remakes them into the Gemini. These creatures have the power to kill and destroy. They can take over or “possess” other humans and thus wreak havoc on </span>
  <span id="freeText4899676848595926190" style="display:none">Gemini Rising by Jessica O’Gorek<br />Gemini Rising: Ethereal Fury by Jessica O’Gorek<br />MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS <br />The main premise in this book is that Mother Earth is furious at humanity’s blatant disregard for the health of the planet and has decided to wipe out mankind. She recruits newly departed souls, generally those who were evil during their lives, and remakes them into the Gemini. These creatures have the power to kill and destroy. They can take over or “possess” other humans and thus wreak havoc on Earth. They plan to destroy towns, cities, and entire nations. <br />Onyx is assigned a mission within a tiny village church and hears a beautiful voice. He goes to investigate, and sees a girl that fascinates him, though he does not understand why. This fascination grows and grows over the course of days until he realizes he has begun to experience emotions again.<br />Violette, the girl Onyx is obsessed with, can sense Onyx’s presence and becomes fascinated herself. She is never frightened of him, in spite of his alien appearance and massive size. <br />The men of the cloth in this church have been fighting “demons” for decades. These demons have slaughtered men, women, and children of the church without mercy, sometimes killing entire congregations at once. The priests know the demons are getting closer, so they are now training Slate in how to detect and battle them. <br />Violette has had a crush on Slate for a very long time. Slate has finally begun to notice her, if only to briefly discuss daily activities with her. Slate has been sheltered his entire life, so social interaction is difficult for him. Onyx possesses Slate so he can be around Violette, while snooping around the church. <br />SPOILERS START HERE:<br />I had several issues with the premise of this novel. Why would Mother Earth focus her battle on the churches? There is no explanation, nor is there any explanation why Mother Earth is so evil she’d slaughter innocents, such as children who have no knowledge of the destruction of the earth. <br />Also, the relationship with Violette and Onyx was disturbing. I disliked the fact that Violette was portrayed as someone who’d want to continue any type of relationship with a being who tried to rape her. I also was offended that the myth of women liking to be raped was perpetuated. This may not have been the author’s intent, but this was distinctly what Violette repeatedly communicated.<br />The author created a good hero in Slate, but then completely demolished him. Slate had strong morals, was intelligent, kind, thoughtful, and brave. This was the person Violette was originally in love with but he was squashed, humiliated, and immolated. Instead, an evil being was offered as a hero. <br />Another issue I had with the book was the comparison of virgins versus non-virgins. Virgins are portrayed as “pure,” good, etc. Violette is a virgin. The implication is that non-virgins are not pure, and they are the destroyers of the world. <br />THE OVERALL SCORE AND WHAT IT MEANS…NO SPOILERS HERE:<br />These issues just decrease the rating of the book for ME. For others, these things may not matter at all. The writing is good. The author has good writing skills and can pull the reader into the story. I simply was distracted by the many questions/issues I discussed above. Perhaps many of these issues will be resolved in the sequel. <br />2 ½ stars rounded up to 3 stars<br />I won this book in a competition. All opinions are my own. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4899676848595926190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3797236-amy-read-to-my-heart-s-content?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657614146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10983541897505103190"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readtomyhearts.blogspot.com/2013/07/book-review-gemini-rising-ethereal-fury.html'>http://readtomyhearts.blogspot.com/20...</a><br/><br/>Looking at the cover, I wasn't too sure if I would like Gemini Rising or not. The cover didn't really incite any strong feelings for me and the blurb made me think it was really too science fiction for me. <br/>But I have been trying to get out of my comfort zone and try new and different stories that I normally would have skimmed over. <br/>I am glad I did pick this one up. <br/><br/>There is so much going on in this book than what the blurb explains, what the cover reveals,</span>
  <span id="freeText10983541897505103190" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readtomyhearts.blogspot.com/2013/07/book-review-gemini-rising-ethereal-fury.html">http://readtomyhearts.blogspot.com/20...</a><br /><br />Looking at the cover, I wasn't too sure if I would like Gemini Rising or not. The cover didn't really incite any strong feelings for me and the blurb made me think it was really too science fiction for me. <br />But I have been trying to get out of my comfort zone and try new and different stories that I normally would have skimmed over. <br />I am glad I did pick this one up. <br /><br />There is so much going on in this book than what the blurb explains, what the cover reveals, and what I even considered it to be about. Yes it does have a little science fiction y aspects to it but nothing that made me want to jump and scream. Actually, it made me look at other scifi stories in a different light now. <br /><br />Then there is the romance factor. It does play a huge part in the story but it is told in a way that makes it seem so innocent and yet alluring at the same time. Violette is like a siren and yet so demure that she has no idea she is this gorgeous human being. The only thing I had a slight problem with was how the male characters: Slate and Onyx, kept switching "woman" and "child" interchangeable together while trying to explain Violette. I guess at the age she was becoming, she could be considered a "woman-child" but it was just uncomfortable when they were lusting after her and then compare her to a child. <br />Other than that, I really liked how the romance progressed through the story. Slate is an okay guy but Onyx is the more interesting one. Slate just seemed so stale to me. But I usually go for the underdog anyways. <br />The plot is a really original and creative one. We hardly ever see Mother Nature personified in a pissed off tone before. Usually, she is the all knowing all understanding one that will always forgive us. <br />Not so with Gemini Rising. She has had enough and sends out her force of Gemini to stop the chaos. And how ironic how she picks out her "killers" to fulfill her demands. Very creative twist! <br />I also enjoyed the religious questions that are raised in the story, Gemini Rising. If the bishop and other lesser priests are supposed to be doing God's work, then why do they have the right to act the way they do. That could be considered a little controversial but I, personally, loved it! I think we should all question everything around us so we can continue to learn about the world. Great job!<br />I also thought it was a great way to tie everything in together on how people came together. And the ending? Let's just say you will be salivating for the next book in the story. Yes, it is one of those endings. One of those where you want to pull your hair out but at the same time, have to give props to the author for leaving it like that. Definitely hooked me!<br /><br />All in all, Gemini Rising is a great read that flows really well and will have you stuck to the pages wanting to see what else Onyx has up his sleeve. I expect big things from Jessica O'Gorek and I know many others will love this original concept with a pretty amazing story line.<br /><br />I give it four hearts~<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10983541897505103190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_954323670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954323670?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/22221379-rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22221379-rebecca?shelf=rar">rar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22221379-rebecca?shelf=kindle-books-i-own">kindle-books-i-own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954323670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7930935812680323418"><br/>**I received this book for free in exchange for an honest review** <br/><br/>Wow, ok I'm not actually 100% sure I understood that but what I did understand was actually very good. I think this may be the kind of book I'm going to have to read more than once to truly get to grips with the story.<br/><br/>The story revolves around onyx and Violett and kind of slate. Onxy is the spirit of a very successful oil tycoon who damaged the earth so severely that once he has died Mother Nature decides to use him to seek venge</span>
  <span id="freeText7930935812680323418" style="display:none"><br />**I received this book for free in exchange for an honest review** <br /><br />Wow, ok I'm not actually 100% sure I understood that but what I did understand was actually very good. I think this may be the kind of book I'm going to have to read more than once to truly get to grips with the story.<br /><br />The story revolves around onyx and Violett and kind of slate. Onxy is the spirit of a very successful oil tycoon who damaged the earth so severely that once he has died Mother Nature decides to use him to seek vengeance on the humans for damaging herself. In order to achieve this she reprograms his mind to work for her and collect other souls in order to build her army. Onxy finds the very few first stages of the transition very difficult and even after that still finds it difficult to do as mother nature wants especially when it comes to harming innocent children, his ultimate rebellion however comes in the form of falling in love with Violett while in the body of slate the young priest to be. Slate is 20 years old and has spent all of his life in the church, while in the church he befriends a young girl Violett who he finds attractive and at the same time is learning all about the 'Demons' possessing humans body's. Slate is the body onyx chooses to possess as a way to learn more about what the church is doing to prevent demon attacks. All the while slate puts up a fight and often tries to protect Violett from onyx who is in his body. Violett is merely a teenager who has not yet completely fallen under the illusion the church is trying to push across. She often questions what the church isn't telling her all the while being extremely attracted to slate and wanting to act on impulse to satisfy her hormonal cravings. The three of them come together in the strangest circumstances and I feel that in the next book these three characters working very much together will bring about the most change.<br /><br />As far as secondary characters go I think there are primarily two groups there is the church and the priests, nuns and bishops who seem very controlling and quite cruel and there is Mother Nature a d her army with all the souls who fight on her side. I have not yet come to. a decision about who is the good / bad side and I'm not sure I will as I really hope in book 2 the three main characters rebelling against both causing all he'll to break loose.<br /><br />In terms of pacing this book was excellent, it is very clear to see that this is the first book in the series as the in depth character descriptions allows the reader to Turkey understand the state the world is In as well as the main conflicts to come without actually having a great deal more happening. It was exactly in my opinion how a first in the series should read easy and fluid.<br /><br />The storyline was great allowing us to really get to know each and every character and what drives them with subtle character developments along the way. I feel I am very much equipped and prepared to read book 2.<br /><br />3.5 stars rating right now due to change depending on how well I understand it after second reading.<br /></span>

<div id="review_625884354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625884354" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7205140-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327251150p2/7205140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/625884354?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/7205140-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17738490-ethereal-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer625884354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3881612045982008253">In this debut book of a new series, Mother Earth is but one word...ticked. She is ticked off that people are so disrespectful to her and are destroying her and her natural beauty with stupid modern ideas. To fix this problem of hers she has created the Gemini, paranormal beings that are out for the blood of those destroying Mother Earth. They were once, themselves, a person who had "great ideas" that only caused Mother Earth damage and heartache. They now, having had their memories wiped, are fi</span>
  <span id="freeText3881612045982008253" style="display:none">In this debut book of a new series, Mother Earth is but one word...ticked. She is ticked off that people are so disrespectful to her and are destroying her and her natural beauty with stupid modern ideas. To fix this problem of hers she has created the Gemini, paranormal beings that are out for the blood of those destroying Mother Earth. They were once, themselves, a person who had "great ideas" that only caused Mother Earth damage and heartache. They now, having had their memories wiped, are fighting with Mother Earth to save and preserve her from future damages. How? By killing off those who are hurting her. They are out for, not only groups of people, but whole towns, cities, and states. They are going to make sure Mother Earth is treated with respect like she should have always been even if that means killing the people that inhabit her. One thing is forbidden, love between a Gemini and a human. When Onyx, one of the Gemini, sees Violette, a human girl, he is drawn to her right away. He knows any kind of relationship is forbidden, but he can't seem to stay away from her. How can he keep this a secret and still do his job for Mother Earth? Is Mother Earth planning to rid herself of all humans? Will Mother Earth inadvertently be destroyed in the mission of saving her? Can love overcome rules?<br /><br />This was a book with a whole new twist to the plot. A plot that I have never read anything like before. This is what makes it a good read from the start, the idea of a "new" kind of read. I think it intrigues the reader from the start with the concept of Mother Earth taking herself back, so to speak. Most paranormal reads now, seem to be all about vampires and/or werewolves, where as this one is about the Gemini; human souls brought to Mother Earth for helping her rid herself of the people harming her. It took me a couple chapters to really get into the book, I must admit, but it was more because it was outside of my "comfort zone" than it was a problem with the book. I was trying to decide in those chapters if it was really a good idea and a worthwhile read. Bottom line was, yes, it was worth the read and a read that, once I gave a chance, I enjoyed. It was so different that I felt like I was reading a whole new genre of book. Not the usual Paranormal read that it was said to be. How can a book be bad when you are dealing with an angry Mother Earth, Gemini, destruction, chaos, and love? The writing was well done, with great flow for most of the book. There were a few times I was confused at first, but was easily put back on track after a few sentences. The characters were unique and fun too. I liked watching them become who they wanted to become. Would I recommend this book to others? You bet I would, if for nothing else but the uniqueness of it all. Will I read on in the series? Probably, it was a good story.<br /><br />4/5 Stars! <br /><br />Received free via author for honest review</span>
  <a data-text-id="3881612045982008253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
